	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Mughal Empire</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Moghul" and "Mughals" redirect here. For the village in Iran, see <a href="/wiki/Moghul,_Iran" title="Moghul, Iran">Moghul, Iran</a>. For the ethnic group, see <a href="/wiki/Mughal_tribe" title="Mughal tribe">Mughal tribe</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">1526-1857 dynastic empire extending over large parts of the Indian subcontinent</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

<div class="NavFrame collapsed" style="border:none;padding:0"><div class="NavHead" style="font-size:105%;background:transparent;text-align:left;background:transparent;text-align:left;padding-right:4em;"><a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Stone_Age" title="South Asian Stone Age">Palaeolithic</a> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047488">.mw-parser-output .nobold{font-weight:normal}</style><span class="nobold">(2,500,000–250,000 BC)</span></div><div class="NavContent" style="font-size:105%;padding:0.2em 0 0.4em;text-align:center"><table style="width:100%;border-collapse:collapse;border-spacing:0px 0px;border:none"><tbody><tr style="vertical-align:top"><td style="text-align:left;"> <a href="/wiki/Madrasian_culture" title="Madrasian culture">Madrasian Culture</a></td><td style="white-space:nowrap;text-align:right;"></td></tr><tr style="vertical-align:top"><td style="text-align:left;"> <a href="/wiki/Soanian" title="Soanian">Soanian Culture</a></td><td style="white-space:nowrap;text-align:right;"></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></td>
</tr><tr><td style="padding:0 0.1em 0.4em">

</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_South_Asia" title="Template:History of South Asia"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_South_Asia" title="Template talk:History of South Asia"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_South_Asia&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Mughal</b> (or <b>Moghul</b>) <b>Empire</b> was an early-modern empire in <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Richards1995-2_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richards1995-2-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> For some two centuries, the empire stretched from the outer fringes of the <a href="/wiki/Indus_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Indus basin">Indus basin</a> in the west, northern <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> in the northwest, and <a href="/wiki/Kashmir" title="Kashmir">Kashmir</a> in the north, to the <a href="/wiki/Highland" title="Highland">highlands</a> of present-day <a href="/wiki/Assam" title="Assam">Assam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> in the east,  and the uplands of the <a href="/wiki/Deccan_plateau" class="mw-redirect" title="Deccan plateau">Deccan plateau</a>  in South India.<sup id="cite_ref-Stein2010-12_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stein2010-12-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> At its greatest extent, it was one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires_in_India" title="List of largest empires in India">largest empires</a> in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_South_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="History of South Asia">history of South Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Peter_2006_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peter_2006-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Mughal Empire is conventionally said to have been founded in 1526 by <a href="/wiki/Babur" title="Babur">Babur</a>, a warrior chieftain from what today is <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, who employed aid from the neighboring <a href="/wiki/Safavid_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Safavid empire">Safavid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman empire">Ottoman</a> empires<sup id="cite_ref-Gilbert2017_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilbert2017-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>  to defeat the <a href="/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate" title="Delhi Sultanate">Sultan of Delhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Lodhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibrahim Lodhi">Ibrahim Lodhi</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Panipat" title="First Battle of Panipat">First Battle of Panipat</a>, and to sweep down the plains of <a href="/wiki/Upper_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Upper India">Upper India</a>. The Mughal imperial structure, however, is sometimes dated to 1600, to the rule of Babur's grandson, <a href="/wiki/Akbar" title="Akbar">Akbar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stein2010-0_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stein2010-0-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  This imperial structure lasted until 1720, until shortly after the death of the last major emperor, <a href="/wiki/Aurengzeb" class="mw-redirect" title="Aurengzeb">Aurengzeb</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Stein2010-1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stein2010-1-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Richards1995-3_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Richards1995-3-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> during whose reign the empire also achieved its maximum geographical extent. The empire subsequently fragmented, reduced to the region in and around <a href="/wiki/Old_Delhi" title="Old Delhi">Old Delhi</a> by the time the British <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">East India Company</a> came to <a href="/wiki/Company_rule_in_India" title="Company rule in India">rule most of India</a>. The empire was formally dissolved by the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">Indian Rebellion of 1857</a>.
</p><p>Although the Mughal Empire was created and sustained by military warfare,<sup id="cite_ref-Stein2010-2_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stein2010-2-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Robb2011_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robb2011-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gilbert2017-2_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gilbert2017-2-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> it did not vigorously suppress the cultures and peoples it came to rule, but rather equalized and placated them through new administrative practices,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and diverse ruling elites, leading to more efficient, centralised, and standardized rule.<sup id="cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-2_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-2-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The relative peace maintained by the empire during much of the 17th century was a factor in India's economic expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-4_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-4-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The main base of the empire's collective wealth was agricultural taxes, instituted by the third Mughal emperor, Akbar.<sup id="cite_ref-Stein2010-3_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stein2010-3-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-1-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Mughal India was also the world leader in manufacturing,<sup id="cite_ref-Parthasarathi_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parthasarathi-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> producing about 25% of the world's industrial output up until the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Williamson_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williamson-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Burgeoning European presence in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, and its increasing demand for Indian raw and finished products, created still greater wealth in the Mughal courts.<sup id="cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-5_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-5-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There was more conspicuous consumption among the Mughal elite,<sup id="cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-6_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-6-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> resulting in greater patronage of <a href="/wiki/Mughal_painting" title="Mughal painting">painting</a>, literary forms, textiles, and <a href="/wiki/Mughal_architecture" title="Mughal architecture">architecture</a>, especially during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Shah_Jahan" title="Shah Jahan">Shah Jahan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AsherTalbot2006-7_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AsherTalbot2006-7-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Among the Mughal <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Sites">UNESCO World Heritage Sites</a> in South Asia are the <a href="/wiki/Agra_Fort" title="Agra Fort">Agra Fort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatehpur_Sikri" title="Fatehpur Sikri">Fatehpur Sikri</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Fort" title="Red Fort">Red Fort</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humayun%27s_Tomb" title="Humayun&#39;s Tomb">Humayun's Tomb</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lahore_Fort" title="Lahore Fort">Lahore Fort</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Taj_Mahal" title="Taj Mahal">Taj Mahal</a>, which is described as "the jewel of Muslim art in India, and one of the universally admired masterpieces of the world's heritage".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
